# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of Grafana's query result caching system and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

The analysis identifies **9 key Go source files** implementing Grafana's query result cache across multiple components:

### Core Architecture Components:

1. **Cache Service Interface** (`pkg/services/caching/service.go`)
   - `CachingService` interface defining cache operations
   - `CachingServiceClient` for request handling with metrics
   - OSS implementation (no-op) vs Enterprise hooks

2. **Cache Key Generation**
   - `GetKey()` function using JSON encoding + SHA256 hashing
   - `JSONEncoder` for deterministic serialization
   - Namespace and prefix support for key organization

3. **Cache Backend Abstraction** (`pkg/infra/remotecache/`)
   - Redis backend (`redis_storage.go`)
   - Memcached backend (`memcached_storage.go`)
   - Database backend (`database_storage.go`)
   - Local in-memory cache (`pkg/infra/localcache/cache.go`)
   - Decorator pattern for encryption and prefixing

4. **TTL Policy Management**
   - 24-hour default TTL
   - Query-specific and panel-level overrides via `QueryCachingConfig`
   - Configurable per datasource

5. **Cache Invalidation**
   - Delete operations on cache storage
   - Event-based invalidation via dashboard save hooks (Enterprise)
   - Metrics tracking for monitoring (HIT/MISS/BYPASS/ERROR statuses)

The answer file contains detailed file listings, symbol definitions, function call chains, and a comprehensive narrative explanation of the entire caching architecture.

Cache Service Interface and Abstraction\\nThe core caching interface is defined in `pkg/services/caching/service.go` with the `CachingService` interface that supports:\\n- `HandleQueryRequest()` - Checks cache for existing query results and returns an update function if cache miss\\n- `HandleResourceRequest()` - Similar caching for resource requests\\n\\nThe OSS implementation (`OSSCachingService`) provides a no-op implementation, while the `CachingServiceClient` wraps this with request handling and metrics collection.\\n\\n### 2. Cache Key Generation\\nCache keys are generated in `pkg/services/caching/service.go::GetKey()` using:\\n- **Namespace and prefix support**: Keys are formatted as `namespace:prefix:hash`\\n- **JSON Encoding**: The `JSONEncoder` struct encodes query objects to JSON using `json.NewEncoder()`\\n- **SHA256 Hashing**: The `SHA256KeyFunc()` function creates a SHA256 hash of the encoded JSON, producing a consistent, collision-resistant key\\n- The encoded key format ensures deterministic cache key generation for identical queries\\n\\n### 3. Cache Backend Abstraction (Redis, Memcached, In-Memory)\\nThe remote cache abstraction is implemented in `pkg/infra/remotecache/` with:\\n\\n**RemoteCache Interface** (`remotecache.go`):\\n- `CacheStorage` interface defines Get/Set/Delete operations for byte arrays\\n- Supports configurable backends via `RemoteCacheSettings` configuration\\n\\n**Backend Implementations**:\\n- **Redis** (`redis_storage.go`): Redis client-based distributed caching\\n- **Memcached** (`memcached_storage.go`): Memcached protocol support\\n- **Database** (`database_storage.go`): SQL database-backed caching for single-instance deployments\\n- **Local In-Memory** (`pkg/infra/localcache/cache.go`): Go-cache based local caching with configurable TTL and cleanup intervals\\n\\n**Decorator Pattern**:\\n- `prefixCacheStorage`: Adds a prefix to all cache keys\\n- `encryptedCacheStorage`: Wraps cache values with encryption/decryption using the secrets service\\n\\n### 4. Cache TTL Policy\\nTTL (Time-To-Live) policies are implemented through:\\n- **Default TTL**: 24 hours (`defaultMaxCacheExpiration`) in `remotecache.go` when not specified\\n- **Query-Specific TTL**: Set via `time.Duration` parameter in `cache.Set()` calls\\n- **Configuration**: Defined in `pkg/setting/setting.go` and `pkg/plugins/models.go::QueryCachingConfig`\\n- **QueryCachingConfig struct**: Contains `Enabled` boolean and `TTLMS` (milliseconds) for datasource-specific caching\\n- **Panel-Level Override**: The `queryCachingTTL` field in dashboard panel queries allows per-query TTL overrides\\n\\n### 5. Cache Invalidation on Dashboard Save\\nCache invalidation follows these patterns:\\n- **Delete Operations**: Cache items are removed via `CacheStorage.Delete(ctx context.Context, key string) error`\\n- **Metrics Tracking**: `pkg/services/caching/metrics.go` tracks cache operations with Prometheus histograms:\\n  - `query_caching_request_duration_seconds` - Query cache performance\\n  - `resource_caching_request_duration_seconds` - Resource cache performance\\n- **Cache Status Headers**: X-Cache header set to HIT/MISS/BYPASS/ERROR/DISABLED values\\n- **Event-Based Invalidation**: Dashboard save events trigger cache invalidation through event bus listeners (Enterprise feature)\\n\\n### 6. Request Flow and Integration\\n**Query Execution Path** (`service.go::WithQueryDataCaching`):\\n1. CachingServiceClient receives a QueryDataRequest\\n2. Calls `HandleQueryRequest()` to check cache\\n3. If cache hit: returns cached response\\n4. If cache miss: executes query via provided function\\n5. Updates cache with result via `UpdateCacheFn` callback\\n6. Sets X-Cache response header with status\\n7. Records metrics for performance monitoring\\n\\n**Response Caching**:\\n- Type: `CachedQueryDataResponse` contains the cached response and an `UpdateCacheFn` callback\\n- Conditional Caching: Uses feature flag `FlagAwsAsyncQueryCaching` to determine when to cache async query results\\n- Error Handling: Only caches successful responses (nil error)\\n\\n### 7. Configuration and Settings\\nCache configuration is managed in:\\n- `pkg/setting/setting.go`: RemoteCacheSettings for backend selection\\n- `conf/defaults.ini` and `conf/sample.ini`: Configuration file templates\\n- Supported backends: `redis`, `memcached`, `database`, `memory`\\n- Encryption support: Optional cache value encryption via secrets service\\n- Prefix support: Configurable key prefix for namespace isolation\\n\\n### 8. Cache Backend Abstraction (Redis, Memcached, In-Memory)\\nThe remote cache abstraction is implemented in `pkg/infra/remotecache/` with:\\n\\n**RemoteCache Interface** (`remotecache.go`):\\n- `CacheStorage` interface defines Get/Set/Delete operations for byte arrays\\n- Supports configurable backends via `RemoteCacheSettings` configuration\\n\\n**Backend Implementations**:\\n- **Redis** (`redis_storage.go`): Redis client-based distributed caching\\n- **Memcached** (`memcached_storage.go`): Memcached protocol support\\n- **Database** (`database_storage.go`): SQL database-backed caching for single-instance deployments\\n- **Local In-Memory** (`pkg/infra/localcache/cache.go`): Go-cache based local caching with configurable TTL and cleanup intervals\\n\\n**Decorator Pattern**:\\n- `prefixCacheStorage`: Adds a prefix to all cache keys\\n- `encryptedCacheStorage`: Wraps cache values with encryption/decryption using the secrets service\\n\\n### 4. Cache TTL Policy\\nTTL (Time-To-Live) policies are implemented through:\\n- **Default TTL**: 24 hours (`defaultMaxCacheExpiration`) in `remotecache.go` when not specified\\n- **Query-Specific TTL**: Set via `time.Duration` parameter in `cache.Set()` calls\\n- **Configuration**: Defined in `pkg/setting/setting.go` and `pkg/plugins/models.go::QueryCachingConfig`\\n- **QueryCachingConfig struct**: Contains `Enabled` boolean and `TTLMS` (milliseconds) for datasource-specific caching\\n- **Panel-Level Override**: The `queryCachingTTL` field in dashboard panel queries allows per-query TTL overrides\\n\\n### 5. Cache Invalidation on Dashboard Save\\nCache invalidation follows these patterns:\\n- **Delete Operations**: Cache items are removed via `CacheStorage.Delete(ctx context.Context, key string) error`\\n- **Metrics Tracking**: `pkg/services/caching/metrics.go` tracks cache operations with Prometheus histograms:\\n  - `query_caching_request_duration_seconds` - Query cache performance\\n  - `resource_caching_request_duration_seconds` - Resource cache performance\\n- **Cache Status Headers**: X-Cache header set to HIT/MISS/BYPASS/ERROR/DISABLED values\\n- **Event-Based Invalidation**: Dashboard save events trigger cache invalidation through event bus listeners (Enterprise feature)\\n\\n### 6. Request Flow and Integration\\n**Query Execution Path** (`service.go::WithQueryDataCaching`):\\n1. CachingServiceClient receives a QueryDataRequest\\n2. Calls `HandleQueryRequest()` to check cache\\n3. If cache hit: returns cached response\\n4. If cache miss: executes query via provided function\\n5. Updates cache with result via `UpdateCacheFn` callback\\n6. Sets X-Cache response header with status\\n7. Records metrics for performance monitoring\\n\\n**Response Caching**:\\n- Type: `CachedQueryDataResponse` contains the cached response and an `UpdateCacheFn` callback\\n- Conditional Caching: Uses feature flag `FlagAwsAsyncQueryCaching` to determine when to cache async query results\\n- Error Handling: Only caches successful responses (nil error)\\n\\n### 7. Configuration and Settings\\nCache configuration is managed in:\\n- `pkg/setting/setting.go`: RemoteCacheSettings for backend selection\\n- `conf/defaults.ini` and `conf/sample.ini`: Configuration file templates\\n- Supported backends: `redis`, `memcached`, `database`, `memory`\\n- Encryption support: Optional cache value encryption via secrets service\\n- Prefix support: Configurable key prefix for namespace isolation\\n\\n### 8. Testing Support\\n- `pkg/services/caching/fake_caching_service.go`: Mock implementation for testing\\n- `pkg/services/caching/service_test.go`: Unit tests covering caching behavior\\n- Remote cache backends have dedicated test files (`*_test.go` and `*_integration_test.go`)\\n\\nThe architecture enables Grafana to efficiently cache query results across multiple datasources while supporting both single-instance deployments (local cache) and distributed deployments (Redis/Memcached), with enterprise features handling cache invalidation tied to dashboard lifecycle events.\"\n}\n",
